<Text>We have been customers of Lee's Donuts for over 30 years! I love their great selection of fresh donuts in all sizes, shapes, and colors. Sizes range from cute little donut holes to huge apple fritters. All are melt-in-your-mouth wonderful!
For those wanting a more substantial meal, they also offer several breakfast selections. Although it can be, at times, a little crowded or noisy, we often met up at Lee's after church for further socialization, as well as a good meal.
Lunch and dinner are covered too - with many sandwich and hamburger choices and several Oriental options. I have enjoyed eating their food and donuts for decades and could never complain about their quality.
The Lee's Donut family is an institution in the North half of Adelanto. I always feel like I am returning to the old days of Adelanto when I see Lee's!<//Text>< Pics>

<name>Ashley Benard</name><Gmap_id>0x80dc7a73e30e9ccd:0xe16516915d671e12<//Gmap_id>< user_id>
117928432353237606469</user_id>
< Date>
1474168738635</Date>
< Rating>
3</Rating>
< text>
I love the location of this park in proximity to my home. My daughters love to come here also.

The Pros:

Benches to sit outside to watch your kids play.

There are grills if you want to come out and cook, play or just hang out. A plus for birthday party's or summer.

There are two baseball diamonds out where  there are regular games going on. You can also come out to practice.

The Cons:

There is no outside lighting by the picnic area or playground . This is a potential threat to people being out here who aren't with a crowd of people. Even in the area where the bleachers are located it is not lighted. Once the baseball field lights turn off, the park is pitch black!!

The bathrooms look like a scary movie inside. Please BYO soap and sanitizer. They're never stocked with tissue and soap
OR towels to dry your hands. The garbage cans are also outside of the restrooms.

The playground is extremely basic for the amount of space this park has. It is not colorful and there are no swings (at a park) I'd suggest that the city add swings and more activities for the children to do to stay busy. Overall, it's a nice place to come to- it just needs these things to be rectified.<//text>

< text>
Their front desk won't bill you correctly based on the copay on your card. They'll under bill you, and then you'll get a bill a month later saying you owe more money.

The only one worth seeing would be Dr McNicoll as he's the only one with in house billing. The others are billed through Adventist Health. Also, their billing department at Alamo Hills is rude and does not seem to understand that they serve people who are sick. The doctors are kind, but their front office is awful and unprofessional.

Edited to add: They do not keep their receptionist staff up to date on who is covering patients when a doctor leaves the practice. They also neglect to put in prescriptions. They also don't honor the exams done by these doctors so you have to go in for a second even though the first was two months ago.

Also, if you require things like birth control, be careful which doctor you see. Some of them don't prescribe it due to religious beliefs.<//text>

<userid>106105890862574393013</userid>< text>
Some great beer to be had here!  (5/5 green stars)
Woods Outbound (to use the official name) is the fifth branch of Woods Beer and a perfect spot to relax after a hike through Golden Gate Park or a trip to the beach. It‚Äôs a tight space, but that‚Äôs sometimes a good thing in a bar and they do also have two fair-sized tables near the window. The young chap behind the bar was very friendly and a testament to what hospitality should be. Beer: we tried 4 of them ($6-$9) and found them all to be interesting and some exceptional ‚Äì for me the standout was the Local Honey ($8). We also had two empanadas ($6 ea.) ‚Äì the Acelga (Swiss chard, gruyere, pine nuts) and Fugazetta (cheese and onion) ‚Äì and felt that the pastry was wonderful but the fillings were a little bit disappointing. The cheese empanada was a little empty ‚Äì we may have received a lemon. It‚Äôs a pity, because I‚Äôve had El Porte√±o‚Äôs alfajores before at the Ferry Building and they were amazing. The beer is perhaps a touch on the pricey side ‚Äì for example, $9 for their Smooch. But considering the ingredients (they put something like 10 lbs of raspberries into each barrel for that beer) it I think it‚Äôs not crazy.

I‚Äôm giving them 5/5 ‚Äúgreen stars‚Äù for social and environmental impact, based on these reasons:

‚Ä¢	Woods are best known for incorporating yerba mate into some of their beer. They source their mate from EcoTeas, who grow it organically, use green energy and are the first ‚Äúwater-neutral‚Äù tea company.
‚Ä¢	Their Morpho beer ($9 for 22 oz. bottle) is an organic herbal ale (also incorporating mate). Organic beer is fairly uncommon ‚Äì some larger breweries (like New Belgium) had trouble selling theirs at the higher price point.
‚Ä¢	Their empanadas are made by El Porte√±o, who tend to use pretty good ingredients (mine had locally-sourced organic chard, others have Prather Ranch grass-fed beef, etc.)
‚Ä¢	Empanadas are served in a simple brown paper bag.
‚Ä¢	Of course, the beer is locally-brewed, reducing transport emissions and carbon footprint.
‚Ä¢	Woods are exploring interesting alternative ingredients for their beer, such as yams.

Interested in writing green star reviews? If so, contact me! (greenstarsproject)< /text>

<Response>None<//Response>< Text>
Some great beer to be had here!  (5/5 green stars)
Woods Outbound (to use the official name) is the fifth branch of Woods Beer and a perfect spot to relax after a hike through Golden Gate Park or a trip to the beach. It‚Äôs a tight space, but that‚Äôs sometimes a good thing in a bar and they do also have two fair-sized tables near the window. The young chap behind the bar was very friendly and a testament to what hospitality should be. Beer: we tried 4 of them ($6-$9) and found them all to be interesting and some exceptional ‚Äì for me the standout was the Local Honey ($8). We also had two empanadas ($6 ea.) ‚Äì the Acelga (Swiss chard, gruyere, pine nuts) and Fugazetta (cheese and onion) ‚Äì and felt that the pastry was wonderful but the fillings were a little bit disappointing. The cheese empanada was a little empty ‚Äì we may have received a lemon. It‚Äôs a pity, because I‚Äôve had El Porte√±o‚Äôs alfajores before at the Ferry Building and they were amazing. The beer is perhaps a touch on the pricey side ‚Äì for example, $9 for their Smooch. But considering the ingredients (they put something like 10 lbs of raspberries into each barrel for that beer) it I think it‚Äôs not crazy.

I‚Äôm giving them 5/5 ‚Äúgreen stars‚Äù for social and environmental impact, based on these reasons:

‚Ä¢	Woods are best known for incorporating yerba mate into some of their beer. They source their mate from EcoTeas, who grow it organically, use green energy and are the first ‚Äúwater-neutral‚Äù tea company.
‚Ä¢	Their Morpho beer ($9 for 22 oz. bottle) is an organic herbal ale (also incorporating mate). Organic beer is fairly uncommon ‚Äì some larger breweries (like New Belgium) had trouble selling theirs at the higher price point.
‚Ä¢	Their empanadas are made by El Porte√±o, who tend to use pretty good ingredients (mine had locally-sourced organic chard, others have Prather Ranch grass-fed beef, etc.)
‚Ä¢	Empanadas are served in a simple brown paper bag.
‚Ä¢	Of course, the beer is locally-brewed, reducing transport emissions and carbon footprint.
‚Ä¢	Woods are exploring interesting alternative ingredients for their beer, such as yams.

Interested in writing green star reviews? If so, contact me! (greenstarsproject)<//Text>

< review>
A few weeks ago, I managed to hydroplane my car into oblivion on the way home from what was otherwise a great weekend. Having lost the car I loved so dearly for the last 12 years, I was thrown into the labyrinth of "way too many options to replace the old Yaris." After test driving a few other models and deciding that the Versa seemed like a good fit for the hatchback-shaped hole in my life, I used the Costco auto program and was put in touch with Future Nissan of Folsom.

I was worried I'd need to dig through promo codes to get an affordable Lyft all the way out to Folsom, since I was carless and am based out of South Sacramento. However, I was please to find that 1) Dana, the dealer I was put in contact with, preferred text communications (thank god), and 2) the dealership will drive out their pre-owned cars to come pick you up so that you can test drive it on the way. Having dealt with a few other dealerships that were pretty skeazy prior to venturing out to Future Nissan, Dana was incredibly nice and easy to talk to, and extremely knowledgeable about the different cars and options they had that would be a good fit for what I was looking for. He was also the one that recommended the car I eventually ended up taking home for good -- a lil white pre-owned Nissan hatchback. I didn't feel like they were ripping me off and was never pressured to buy while I was browsing the inventory, and Dana was very honest with his opinions about which cars would be the best fit for my lifestyle and budget.

The dealership also helped with setting me up with the bank loan and processing all the paperwork, which was incredibly easy to do (thanks Brian!). I didn't think I was going to end up signing up for the maintenance /warranty plan, but the customer service was so good that I'd rather come back out there than have to navigate through the auto garages I've dealt with in the past. And they provide you with a rental for free while your car is being serviced. Pretty raaaad!

Anyways, check them out. I'm definitely talking them up to my friends, maybe you will too :) And loving my new lil car, it's exactly what I was looking for.<//review>

< Review>
My car buying experience started with Sam over the phone. I told Sam what I was looking for and the price that I was willing to pay. Sam said that Future Nissan of Folsom (FNOF) would not lose a deal over price. Sam invited me to come test drive the car that I was interested in and he guaranteed that we would have fun and laugh at the very least.

We decided to accept Sam's offer. My wife and I were greeted by a manager named Joseph when we arrived. Joseph was very well dressed, friendly and professional. Joseph invited us to relax and enjoy a coffee while we waited for Sam to pull the car around.

Sam made good on his promise about having fun. Sam was extremely outgoing, funny and knowledgeable. Sam's low-pressure approach was reassuring and made the car buying experience enjoyable.

Once we agreed to purchase the car, Joseph stopped by to discuss the price, financing, and other options. Joseph was very professional and ultimately approved an amazing deal for a certified pre-owned vehicle.

I would be remiss if I did not mention the front desk manager Kyle who was an integral part of this deal. He was also well dressed, professional, friendly, and a pleasure to work with.

The last stop at any dealership is the finance department where you normally get the hard sell on extended warranties and other options, but not at FNOF. Like the front of the house, the finance department was friendly, professional and low pressure.

Last but not least is Gary who is also a manager. Gary helped me resolve a problem a few days after the sale. Gary was patient, understanding and professional like the rest of the team. I normally wouldn't expect to receive such excellent customer service after driving a used car off the lot, but Gary really went the extra mile to make sure that I was satisfied.

I recommend FNOF to anyone in the market for a new or used car.<//Review>
